<p>Since June 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-addict_3-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-addict-3">[3]</a></sup> TED Talks had been offered for free viewing online, under an Attribution-NonCommercial-NoDerivatives <a title="Creative Commons license" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creative_Commons_license">Creative Commons license</a>, through TED.com.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> As of December&nbsp;2020 over 3,500 talks are freely available on the official website.<sup id="cite_ref-numbertalks_19-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-numbertalks-19">[19]</a></sup> In June 2011, TED Talks' combined viewing figures surpassed 500 million,<sup id="cite_ref-mashable.com_20-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-mashable.com-20">[20]</a></sup> and by November 2012, they had been watched over one billion times worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-billion_21-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-billion-21">[21]</a></sup> While the talks are available free online, sharing TED content in commercial contexts (such as corporate learning and talent development) requires a license.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="History" class="mw-headline">History</span></h2>
<h3><span id="1984.E2.80.931999:_Founding_and_early_years"></span><span id="1984&ndash;1999:_Founding_and_early_years" class="mw-headline">1984&ndash;1999: Founding and early years</span></h3>
<div class="thumbinner" style="width: 222px;"><a class="image" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton_talking_at_TED_2007.jpg"><img class="thumbimage" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Bill_Clinton_talking_at_TED_2007.jpg/220px-Bill_Clinton_talking_at_TED_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Bill_Clinton_talking_at_TED_2007.jpg/330px-Bill_Clinton_talking_at_TED_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Bill_Clinton_talking_at_TED_2007.jpg/440px-Bill_Clinton_talking_at_TED_2007.jpg 2x" width="220" height="165" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960"></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify">&nbsp;</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width: 222px;">
<div class="thumbcaption"><a title="Bill Clinton" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> addresses TED, 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>TED was conceived in 1984 by Emmy-winning broadcast and graphic designer <a title="Harry Marks (broadcast designer)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Marks_(broadcast_designer)">Harry Marks</a>, who observed convergence of the fields of technology, entertainment, and design ("TED"). He approached architect and graphic designer <a title="Richard Saul Wurman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Saul_Wurman">Richard Saul Wurman</a>, who agreed on condition that he would be a co-founder.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The first conference, organized by Marks and Wurman with help from Frank Stanton, featured demos of the <a title="Compact disc" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compact_disc">compact disc</a>, co-developed by <a title="Philips" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philips">Philips</a> and <a title="Sony" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sony">Sony</a>, and one of the first demonstrations of the <a class="mw-redirect" title="Apple Macintosh" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Macintosh">Apple Macintosh</a> computer.<sup id="cite_ref-addict_3-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-addict-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forum_24-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-forum-24">[24]</a></sup> Presentations were given by the mathematician <a title="Benoit Mandelbrot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benoit_Mandelbrot">Benoit Mandelbrot</a> and others such as <a title="Nicholas Negroponte" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicholas_Negroponte">Nicholas Negroponte</a> and <a title="Stewart Brand" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stewart_Brand">Stewart Brand</a>. The event was financially unsuccessful; six years elapsed before a second conference was organised.<sup id="cite_ref-ted.com_25-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-ted.com-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>TED2 was held at the same Monterey Conference Center in California in 1990. From 1990 onward, a growing community of "TEDsters" gathered annually with Wurman leading the conference in Monterey until 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> when it was moved to <a title="Long Beach, California" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Long_Beach,_California">Long Beach, California</a> due to a substantial increase in the number of those attending.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LATimes_28-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-LATimes-28">[28]</a></sup> Speakers were initially drawn from the fields of expertise behind the acronym TED; but during the 1990s, presenters broadened to include scientists, philosophers, musicians, religious leaders, philanthropists, and many others.<sup id="cite_ref-ted.com_25-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-ted.com-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="2000.E2.80.93present:_Recent_growth"></span><span id="2000&ndash;present:_Recent_growth" class="mw-headline">2000&ndash;present: Recent growth</span></h3>
<p>In 2000, Wurman, looking for a successor at age 65, met with new-media entrepreneur and TED enthusiast <a title="Chris Anderson (entrepreneur)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Anderson_(entrepreneur)">Chris Anderson</a> to discuss future happenings. Anderson's UK media company <a title="Future plc" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Future_plc">Future</a> bought TED. In November 2001, Anderson's non-profit The <a title="Sapling Foundation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sapling_Foundation">Sapling Foundation</a> (motto: "fostering the spread of great ideas")<sup id="cite_ref-howtedworks_1-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-howtedworks-1">[1]</a></sup> acquired TED from Future for &pound;6m.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In February 2002, Anderson gave a TED Talk in which he explained his vision of the conference and his future role of <a title="Curator" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curator">curator</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Wurman left after the 2002 conference.</p>
<p>In 2006, attendance cost was $4,400 per person and was by invitation only.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The membership model was shifted in January 2007 to an annual membership fee of $6,000, which included attendance of the conference, club mailings, networking tools, and conference DVDs. The 2018 conference was $10,000 per attendee.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between 2001 and 2006, TED upgraded its platform to provide TED talks online for free, added TEDGlobal that became a worldwide conference, and created the TED Prize.</p>
<p>In 2014, the conference was moved to Vancouver, British Columbia, Canada.</p>
<p>TED is currently funded by various revenue streams, including attendance fees, corporate sponsorships, foundation support, licensing fees, and book sales. Corporate sponsors are diverse, including companies such as <a title="Google" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google">Google</a>, <a title="General Electric" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Electric">GE</a>, <a title="AOL" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AOL">AOL</a>, <a title="Goldman Sachs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goldman_Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a>, and <a title="The Coca-Cola Company" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Coca-Cola_Company">The Coca-Cola Company</a>. Sponsors do not participate in the event's creation, nor are they allowed to present on the main stage.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-americanu_34-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-americanu-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, TED staff consisted of about 180 people headquartered in <a title="New York City" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_City">New York City</a> and <a title="Vancouver" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, British Columbia.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> On July 1, 2019, the TED Conferences LLC was transferred from Sapling Foundation to TED Foundation to "align with our brand and make it easier for our donors to connect TED donations to TED Conferences, LLC."<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>At TED 2015, <a title="Bill Gates" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Gates">Bill Gates</a> warned that the world was not prepared for the next pandemic, a situation that occurred in late 2019 with the <a title="COVID-19 pandemic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2021, TED launched the TED Audio Collective with a number of podcasts featuring previous TED Talks and other relevant topics.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>TED 2022 was held in <a title="Vancouver" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vancouver">Vancouver</a>. There was criticism after <a title="Marvin Rees" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvin_Rees">Marvin Rees</a>, <a title="Mayor of Bristol" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mayor_of_Bristol">Mayor of Bristol</a>, flew 9,200 miles (14,800&nbsp;km) to speak about <a title="Climate change" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change">climate change</a> and the need for reduced <a class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon emission" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_emission">carbon emissions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-61596817_40-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-BBC-61596817-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="TED_Prize" class="mw-headline">TED Prize</span></h2>
<p>The TED Prize was introduced in 2005. Until 2010, $100,000 was given annually to three individuals with a "wish to change the world".<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Each winner unveiled their wish at the main annual conference. Since 2010, a single winner has been chosen to ensure that TED can maximize its efforts in achieving the winner's wish. In 2012, the prize was not awarded to a person, but to a concept connected to the current global phenomenon of increasing <a title="Urbanization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urbanization">urbanization</a>. In 2013, the prize amount was increased to $1 million.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> TED Prize winners in previous years have been:</p>

<p>TED Conference commissioned New York artist <a title="Tom Shannon (artist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tom_Shannon_(artist)">Tom Shannon</a> to create a prize sculpture for all TED Prize winners. It consists of an eight-inch-diameter (20&nbsp;cm) aluminum sphere magnetically levitated above a walnut disc. As of 2018 the prize has been recast as <a title="The Audacious Project" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Audacious_Project">The Audacious Project</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="TED.com" class="mw-headline">TED.com</span></h2>
<p>In 2005, Chris Anderson hired <a title="June Cohen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/June_Cohen">June Cohen</a> as Director of TED Media. In June 2006, after Cohen's idea of a TV show based on TED lectures was rejected by several networks, a selection of talks that had received highest audience ratings was posted on the websites of TED, <a title="YouTube" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YouTube">YouTube</a> and <a title="ITunes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ITunes">iTunes</a> under <a title="Creative Commons license" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creative_Commons_license">Creative Commons</a> Attribution-NonCommercial-NoDerivs 3.0.<sup id="cite_ref-giving_60-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-giving-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Only a handful of talks was initially posted to see if there was an audience for them. In January of the following year, the number of talks on the sites had grown to 44, and they had been viewed more than three million times. On the basis of that success, the organization pumped hundreds of thousands of dollars into its video production operations and the development of a website to feature about 100 of the talks.<sup id="cite_ref-giving_60-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-giving-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CFP_62-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-CFP-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2007, the new TED.com was launched, developed by New York and San Francisco-based design company <a title="Method (company)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Method_(company)">Method</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The website has won many prizes, including seven <a class="mw-redirect" title="Webby Award" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Webby_Award">Webby Awards</a>, iTunes' "Best Podcast of the Year" (2006&ndash;2010); the <em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Communication Arts (magazine)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communication_Arts_(magazine)">Communication Arts</a></em> Interactive Award for Information Design (2007); the OMMA Award for Video Sharing, the Web Visionary Award for Technical Achievement, and <a title="The One Club" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_One_Club">The One Show Interactive</a> Bronze Award (2008); the <a class="mw-redirect" title="AIGA" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AIGA">AIGA</a> Annual Design Competition (2009); and a <a class="mw-redirect" title="Peabody Award" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peabody_Award">Peabody Award</a> (2012).<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2009, TED videos had been viewed 50 million times. In June 2011, they reached 500 million views;<sup id="cite_ref-mashable.com_20-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-mashable.com-20">[20]</a></sup> and on November 13, 2012, they reached their billionth video view.<sup id="cite_ref-billion_21-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-billion-21">[21]</a></sup> In March 2012, Chris Anderson said in an interview:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>It used to be 800 people getting together once a year; now it's about a million people a day watching TED Talks online. When we first put up a few of the talks as an experiment, we got such impassioned responses that we decided to flip the organization on its head and think of ourselves not so much as a conference but as "ideas worth spreading," building a big website around it. The conference is still the engine, but the website is the amplifier that takes the ideas to the world.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite">&mdash;&thinsp;<cite>Chris Anderson,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>In March 2012, <a title="Netflix" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netflix">Netflix</a> announced a deal to <a title="Streaming media" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Streaming_media">stream</a> an initial series of 16 two-hour collections of TED Talks on similar subjects. It was made available to subscribers in the United States, Canada, Latin America, the United Kingdom, and Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Hosted by Jami Floyd, <em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#TED.com">TED Talks NYC</a></em> debuted on <a title="NYC Media" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NYC_Media">NYC Life</a> on March 21, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of October 2020, over 3500 TED talks had been posted,<sup id="cite_ref-numbertalks_19-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-numbertalks-19">[19]</a></sup> and five to seven new talks are published each week. On TED.com, most talks and speakers are introduced, and talk transcripts are provided; some talks also have footnotes and resource lists.</p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>
<h3><span id="TEDGlobal" class="mw-headline">TEDGlobal</span></h3>
<p>In 2005, under Anderson's supervision, a more internationally oriented sister conference was added, under the name TEDGlobal. It was held, in chronological order: in <a title="Oxford" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford">Oxford</a>, UK (2005), in <a title="Arusha" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arusha">Arusha</a>, Tanzania (2007, titled TEDAfrica), in Oxford again (2009 and 2010), and in <a title="Edinburgh" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>, UK (2011, 2012, and 2013). In 2014, it was held in <a class="mw-redirect" title="Rio de Janeiro, Brazil" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro,_Brazil">Rio de Janeiro, Brazil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Additionally, there was TED India, in <a title="Mysore" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mysore">Mysore</a> (2009) and TEDGlobal London in <a title="London" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London">London</a> (2015).<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> TEDGlobal 2017 was held again in Arusha, Tanzania, and it was curated and hosted by Emeka Okafor.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>TED's European director (and curator of TEDGlobal) is Swiss-born <a title="Bruno Giussani" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bruno_Giussani">Bruno Giussani</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>The TED 2011 conference, <em>The Rediscovery of Wonder</em>, was held in <a title="Long Beach, California" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Long_Beach,_California">Long Beach, California</a>, US, from February 28 to March 4, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-redorbit.com_76-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-redorbit.com-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The TED conference has a companion conference, TEDGlobal, held in the UK each summer. The 2009 TEDGlobal, <em>The Substance of Things Not Seen</em>, was held in Oxford, July 21&ndash;24, 2009. 2010's TEDGlobal (again in Oxford) was themed <em>And Now The Good News</em>; in 2011 the conference moved to a new home in Edinburgh and was held July 12&ndash;15 with the theme <em>The Stuff Of Life</em>. The 2012 TEDGlobal conference <em>Radical Openness</em> was held in Edinburgh, June 25&ndash;29.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="TED_Translators" class="mw-headline">TED Translators</span></h3>
<p>TED Translators, formerly known as the Open Translation Project (OTP), started as the TED Open Translation Project in May 2009. It intends to "[reach] out to the 4.5 billion people on the planet who don't speak English", according to TED Curator Chris Anderson.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> The OTP used crowd-based subtitling platforms to translate the text of TED and TED-Ed videos, as well as to caption and translate videos created in the TEDx program. (Until May 2012 it worked with its technology partner dotSUB, and then with the <a title="Open-source software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open-source_software">open source</a> translation tool <a class="mw-redirect" title="Amara (subtitling)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amara_(subtitling)">Amara</a>). When the project was launched, 300 translations had been completed in 40 languages by 200 volunteer transcribers.<sup id="cite_ref-redorbit.com_76-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-redorbit.com-76">[76]</a></sup> By May 2015, more than 70,000 sets of subtitles in 107 languages<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> had been completed by (an all-time total of) 38,173 volunteer translators.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>The project helped generate a significant increase in international visitors to TED's website. Traffic from outside the US has increased 350 percent: there has been 600 percent growth in Asia, and more than 1000 percent in South America.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Members have several tools dedicated to knowledge management, such as the OTP Wiki OTPedia, Facebook groups, or video tutorials.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="TEDx" class="mw-headline">TEDx</span></h3>
<p>TEDx are independent events similar to TED in presentation. They can be organized by anyone who obtains a free license from TED, and agrees to follow certain principles.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> TEDx events are required to be non-profit, but organizers may use an admission fee or commercial sponsorship to cover costs.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Speakers are not paid and must also relinquish the copyrights to their materials, which TED may edit and distribute under a <a title="Creative Commons" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creative_Commons">Creative Commons</a> license.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of January 2014, the TEDxTalks library contained some 30,000 films and presentations from more than 130 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> As of October 2017, the TEDx archive surpassed 100,000 talks.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> In March 2013, eight TEDx events were organised every day; raised up from five in June 2012, the previous year, in 133 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-listen_91-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-listen-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-a_fresh_take_92-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-a_fresh_take-92">[92]</a></sup> TEDx presentations may include live performances, which are catalogued in the <a title="TEDx Music Project" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TEDx_Music_Project">TEDx Music Project</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2011, TED began a program called "TEDx in a Box", which is intended to enable people in developing countries to hold TEDx events. TEDx also expanded to include TEDxYouth events, TEDx corporate events, and TEDxWomen.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space: nowrap;">[<em><a title="Wikipedia:Citation needed" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></em>]</sup> TEDxYouth events are independent programs set up for students who are in grades 7&ndash;12.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> These events usually have audiences of people close to the age of the students and sometimes show TED Talks.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space: nowrap;">[<em><a title="Wikipedia:Citation needed" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></em>]</sup> According to <a title="TEDxSanta Cruz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TEDxSanta_Cruz">TEDxSanta Cruz</a>, "as of 2015, over 1,500 [TEDx events] have been scheduled all over the world."<sup id="cite_ref-TEDxSantaCruz_2015_95-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-TEDxSantaCruz_2015-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>TEDx events have evolved over time. Events such as TEDxBeaconStreet created TEDx Adventures for participants. People may sign up for free, hands-on experiences in their local communities, led by an expert.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>A TEDx youth event license follows the same format as the standard event license and falls within the same TEDx event rules, except this event is oriented towards youth. TEDxYouth licenses may be held by youth, adults, or a combination of both. For events held at schools, the license must be held by a current student, faculty, or staff member. The first TEDxYouth event was held by TEDxYouth@Tokyo in Japan.</p>
<h3><span id="TED_Fellows" class="mw-headline">TED Fellows</span></h3>
<div class="thumbinner" style="width: 222px;"><a class="image" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:TEDGlobal2012.jpg"><img class="thumbimage" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/TEDGlobal2012.jpg/220px-TEDGlobal2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/TEDGlobal2012.jpg/330px-TEDGlobal2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/TEDGlobal2012.jpg/440px-TEDGlobal2012.jpg 2x" width="220" height="330" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="3000"></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify">&nbsp;</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width: 222px;">
<div class="thumbcaption">TEDGlobal 2012 at the <a title="Edinburgh International Conference Centre" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edinburgh_International_Conference_Centre">Edinburgh International Conference Centre</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>TED Fellows were introduced in 2007, during the first TEDAfrica conference in <a title="Arusha" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arusha">Arusha</a>, Tanzania, where 100 young people were selected from across the continent. Two years later, during TEDIndia, 99 Fellows were recruited, mainly from South Asia.</p>
<p>In 2009, the Fellows program was initiated in its present form. For every TED or TEDGlobal conference, 20 Fellows are selected; a total of 40 new Fellows a year. Each year, 20 past Fellows are chosen to participate in the two-year Senior Fellows program (in which they will attend four more conferences).</p>
<p>2019 marked the tenth anniversary of the TED Fellows program.</p>
<p>Acceptance as a Fellow is not based on academic <a title="Credential" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Credential">credentials</a>, but mainly on past and current actions, and plans for the future.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Besides attending a conference free of charge, each Fellow takes part in a special program with <a title="Mentorship" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mentorship">mentoring</a> by experts in the field of spreading ideas, and he or she can give a short talk on the "TED Fellows" stage. Some of these talks are subsequently published on TED.com. Senior Fellows have additional benefits and responsibilities.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="TED-Ed" class="mw-headline">TED-Ed</span></h3>
<p>TED-Ed is a <a title="YouTube" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YouTube">YouTube</a> channel from Ted which creates short animated educational videos. It also has its own website.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> TED-Ed lessons are created in collaboration with educators and animators. Current advisers for Ted-Ed lessons include <a title="Aaron Sams" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aaron_Sams">Aaron Sams</a>, Jackie Bezos, John Hunter, <a title="Jonathan Bergmann" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_Bergmann">Jonathan Bergmann</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" title="Melinda Gates" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melinda_Gates">Melinda French Gates</a>, and <a title="Sal Khan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sal_Khan">Sal Khan</a>. It has over 17.8 million subscribers and over 3.3 billion views as of November 2022.</p>
<h3><span id="TED_Audio_Collective" class="mw-headline">TED Audio Collective</span></h3>
<p>The <a class="external text" href="https://audiocollective.ted.com/" rel="nofollow">TED Audio Collective</a> is a collection of podcasts for the curious with over 25 shows.</p>
<p>One of those shows is the TED Interview <a title="Podcast" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Podcast">podcast</a> which launched on October 16, 2018, during which <a title="Chris Anderson (entrepreneur)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Anderson_(entrepreneur)">Chris Anderson</a> holds conversations<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> with speakers who have previously given a <a title="List of TED speakers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_TED_speakers">TED talk</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> providing the guest a chance to speak in greater depth about their background, projects, motivation,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> re-evaluation of past experiences,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> or plans for the future.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space: nowrap;">[<em><a title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (October 2022)">needs update</span></a></em>]</sup></p>
<p>Each interview lasts between 45 minutes and about one hour. All podcasts are available on the TED website, in part together with transcripts, as well as through platforms such as <a title="ITunes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ITunes#Podcasts">Apple Podcasts</a>, <a title="Spotify" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spotify">Spotify</a>, <a title="Google Podcasts" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google_Podcasts">Google Podcasts</a>, <a title="TuneIn" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TuneIn">TuneIn</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" title="Stitcher Radio" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stitcher_Radio">Stitcher</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" title="RadioPublic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RadioPublic">RadioPublic</a>, <a title="Castbox" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Castbox">Castbox</a>, <a title="IHeartRadio" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IHeartRadio">iHeartRadio</a>, and <a title="BBC Radio 4 Extra" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC_Radio_4_Extra">BBC Radio 4 Extra</a>.</p>
<p>Season Four began in March 2020 during the <a title="COVID-19 pandemic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> as a live-stream broadcast co-hosted by Chris Anderson and Whitney Pennington Rodgers and often offered listeners the opportunity to submit questions to the speaker.</p>

<h3><span id="TEDMED" class="mw-headline">TEDMED</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a title="TEDMED" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TEDMED">TEDMED</a></div>
<p><a title="TEDMED" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TEDMED">TEDMED</a> is an annual conference concerned with health and medicine. It is an independent event operating under license from the nonprofit TED conference.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_162-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-:0-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>TEDMED was founded in 1998 by TED's founder Ricky Wurman. After years of inactivity, in 2008 Wurman sold TEDMED to entrepreneur <a title="Marc Hodosh" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marc_Hodosh">Marc Hodosh</a>, who recreated and relaunched it. The first event under Hodosh's ownership was held in San Diego in October 2009. In January 2010, TED.com began including videos of TEDMED talks on the TED website.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_162-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-:0-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>The second Hodosh-owned edition of TEDMED took place in October 2010, also in San Diego. It sold out for a second year and attracted notable healthcare leaders and Hollywood celebrities.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2011, <a title="Jay S. Walker" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jay_S._Walker">Jay Walker</a> and a group of executives and investors purchased TEDMED from Hodosh for $16 million with future additional payments of as much as $9 million. The conference was then moved to Washington, DC.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="TEDWomen" class="mw-headline">TEDWomen</span></h3>
<p>TEDWomen is an annual three-day conference.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> Established in 2010, TEDWomen features speakers focused on women-oriented themes, including gender issues and reproductive health.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> There are over 130 TEDWomen Talks available<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> to watch on the TED website. Past speakers include former president <a title="Jimmy Carter" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Carter">Jimmy Carter</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> <a title="Hillary Clinton" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hillary_Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> <a title="Sheryl Sandberg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheryl_Sandberg">Sheryl Sandberg</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> <a title="Madeleine Albright" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madeleine_Albright">Madeleine Albright</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> <a title="Nancy Pelosi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nancy_Pelosi">Nancy Pelosi</a><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> and <a title="Halla T&oacute;masd&oacute;ttir" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Halla_T%C3%B3masd%C3%B3ttir">Halla T&oacute;masd&oacute;ttir</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="TEDYouth" class="mw-headline">TEDYouth</span></h3>
<p>TEDYouth talks are aimed at middle school and high school students and feature information from youth innovators.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Other_programs" class="mw-headline">Other programs</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><strong>TED@Work</strong> &mdash; A program that leverages TED content to inspire new ways of working in professional settings. This program provides ways for organizations and companies to license TED content for use in learning and talent development contexts.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></li>
<li><strong>TED Books</strong> &mdash; These are original books from TED. The initiative began in January 2011 as an ebook series and re-launched in September 2014 with its first book in print.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></li>
<li><strong>TedEd Clubs</strong> &mdash; An education based initiative to get young people (ages 8 to 18) to share their ideas with peers and others by giving a TED-like presentation on a topic. TED provides curricula and limited support for the Clubs free of charge.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></li>
<li><strong>TED Salon</strong> &mdash; Smaller evening-length events with speakers and performers.<sup id="cite_ref-Conferences_180-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-Conferences-180">[180]</a></sup></li>
<li><em><strong><a title="TED Radio Hour" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_Radio_Hour">TED Radio Hour</a></strong></em> &mdash; A radio program,<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> with audio downloads and a podcast <a title="RSS" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RSS">RSS</a> feed,<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> hosted by <a title="Manoush Zomorodi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manoush_Zomorodi">Manoush Zomorodi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-npr.org--about-npr-776132106_183-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-npr.org--about-npr-776132106-183">[183]</a></sup> previously <a title="Guy Raz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guy_Raz">Guy Raz</a> and co-produced with <a title="NPR" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NPR">NPR</a>. Each episode uses multiple TED Talks to examine a common theme.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> Originated and executive produced by Deron Triff and <a title="June Cohen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/June_Cohen">June Cohen</a>, the first episode was broadcast in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></li>
<li><em><strong>TEDx Talks</strong></em> is a YouTube channel<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> which is ranked No. 1 globally for a non profit (2021).<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> The channel has approximately 30m subscribers and 800m views with estimated revenues of between $24.5K &ndash; $391.6K monthly.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></li>
<li><em><strong>TED Countdown</strong></em> is a global initiative, powered by TED and Future Stewards, to accelerate solutions to the climate crisis. The goal: to build a better future by cutting greenhouse gas emissions in half by 2030 towards reaching net zero by 2050. Launched 2020 online, summit 2021 in Edinburgh, Scotland.</li>
<li>TED also offers other podcasts such as <em>Sincerely, X</em> (featuring anonymous TED Talks)<sup id="cite_ref-:2_191-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-:2-191">[191]</a></sup> and <em>Work / Life</em> which discusses creative workplaces.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="Criticism" class="mw-headline">Criticism</span></h2>
<h3><span id="Pricing" class="mw-headline">Pricing</span></h3>
<p>Frank Swain, a journalist, refused to participate in a TEDx event without being paid. He said that it was unacceptable that TED, a non-profit organization, charged attendees $6,000 but prohibited organisers of the smaller, independently organized TEDx events from paying speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> Speakers and performers at official TED events are not compensated.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p><a title="Sarah Lacy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sarah_Lacy">Sarah Lacy</a> of <em><a class="mw-redirect" title="BusinessWeek" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BusinessWeek">BusinessWeek</a></em> and <em><a title="TechCrunch" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TechCrunch">TechCrunch</a></em> wrote in 2010 that TED attendees complained of elitism from a "hierarchy of parties throughout the LA area with strict lists and security" after the sessions. She gave TED credit for freely live-streaming and posting videos of its talks.<sup id="cite_ref-techcrunch.com_195-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-techcrunch.com-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="TED_Talk_content" class="mw-headline">TED Talk content</span></h3>
<p>Disagreements have also occurred between TED speakers and organizers. In her 2010 TED Talk, comedian <a title="Sarah Silverman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sarah_Silverman">Sarah Silverman</a> referred to adopting a "retarded" child. TED organizer <a title="Chris Anderson (entrepreneur)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Anderson_(entrepreneur)">Chris Anderson</a> objected via his <a title="Twitter" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twitter">Twitter</a> account, leading to a Twitter skirmish between them.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also in 2010, statistician <a class="mw-redirect" title="Nassim Taleb" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nassim_Taleb">Nassim Taleb</a> called TED a "monstrosity that turns scientists and thinkers into low-level entertainers, like circus performers". He claimed TED curators did not initially post his talk "warning about the financial crisis" on their site on purely cosmetic grounds.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2012, venture capitalist <a title="Nick Hanauer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nick_Hanauer">Nick Hanauer</a> spoke at <a class="new" title="TED University (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=TED_University&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">TED University</a>, challenging the belief that top income earners in America were the engines of job creation. TED attracted controversy when it chose not to post Hanauer's talk on their website. His talk analysed the top rate of tax versus unemployment and economic equality.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> TED was accused of censoring the talk by not posting it.<sup id="cite_ref-IBT_200-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-IBT-200">[200]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 7, 2012, TED curator Chris Anderson, in an email to Hanauer, commented on his decision and took issue with several of Hanauer's assertions in the talk, including the idea that businesspeople were not job creators. He also made clear his aversion to the talk's "political nature":<sup id="cite_ref-email_202-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-email-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>I agree with your language about ecosystems, and your dismissal of some of the mechanistic economy orthodoxy, yet many of your own statements seem to go further than those arguments justify.<br>But even if the talk was rated a home run, we couldn't release it, because it would be unquestionably regarded as out and out political. We're in the middle of an election year in the US. Your argument comes down firmly on the side of one party. And you even reference that at the start of the talk. TED is nonpartisan and is fighting a constant battle with TEDx organizers to respect that principle...<br>Nick, I personally share your disgust at the growth in inequality in the US, and would love to have found a way to give people a clearer mindset on the issue, without stoking a tedious partisan rehash of all the arguments we hear every day in the mainstream media.<br>Alas, my judgement is that publishing your talk would not meet that goal.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite">&mdash;&thinsp;<cite><a title="Chris Anderson (entrepreneur)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Anderson_(entrepreneur)">Chris Anderson</a>, May 7, 2012<sup id="cite_ref-email_202-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-email-202">[202]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>The <em><a title="National Journal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Journal">National Journal</a></em> reported that Anderson considered Hanauer's talk one of the most politically controversial they had produced, and they needed to be careful about when they posted it.<sup id="cite_ref-IBT_200-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-IBT-200">[200]</a></sup> Anderson responded on his personal blog that TED posted only one talk each day, selected from many.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> <em><a title="Forbes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forbes">Forbes</a></em> staff writer Bruce Upbin described Hanauer's talk as "shoddy and dumb"<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> while <em><a title="New York (magazine)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_(magazine)">New York</a></em> magazine condemned TED's move.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following a TEDx talk by parapsychologist <a title="Rupert Sheldrake" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rupert_Sheldrake">Rupert Sheldrake</a>, TED issued a statement saying their scientific advisors believed that "there is little evidence for some of Sheldrake's more radical claims", and recommended that it "should not be distributed without being framed with caution". The video was moved from the TEDx YouTube channel to the TED blog, accompanied by such framing language. This prompted accusations of censorship, which TED rebutted by pointing out that Sheldrake's talk was still on their website.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> A 2013 talk by <a title="Graham Hancock" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graham_Hancock">Graham Hancock</a>, promoting the use of the drug <a title="N,N-Dimethyltryptamine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/N,N-Dimethyltryptamine">DMT</a>, was treated the same way.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-a_fresh_take_92-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-a_fresh_take-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to professor <a title="Benjamin H. Bratton" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_H._Bratton">Benjamin Bratton</a> at <a title="University of California, San Diego" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_California,_San_Diego">University of California, San Diego</a>, TED Talks' efforts at fostering progress in <a class="mw-redirect" title="Socio-economics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socio-economics">socio-economics</a>, science, philosophy and technology have been ineffective.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> Chris Anderson responded that some critics misunderstood TED's goals, failing to recognise that it aimed to instill excitement in audiences in the same ways speakers felt it. He said that TED wished only to bring awareness of significant topics to larger audiences.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="In_popular_culture" class="mw-headline">In popular culture</span></h2>
<p>The <a title="Alien (franchise)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alien_(franchise)"><em>Alien</em> franchise</a> features a fictional portrayal of a 2023 TED Conference, in the form of a <a title="Alien (franchise)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alien_(franchise)#Short_films">short film</a> called "The Peter Weyland Files: TED Conference, 2023".<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> It was a part of the <a class="mw-redirect" title="TED 2023" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_2023">viral marketing campaign</a> for the franchise's film <a title="Prometheus (2012 film)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prometheus_(2012_film)"><em>Prometheus</em></a> (2012).</p>
